</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">
<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Europe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/32px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/48px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/64px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:European_Union" title="Portal:European Union">European Union&#32;portal</a> <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li>
<li><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Atlas_of_European_Union" class="extiw" title="commons:Atlas of European Union">Atlas</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There are five recognised candidates for future <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">membership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Turkey</a> (applied on 14 April 1987), <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Macedonia to the European Union">Macedonia</a> (applied on 22 March 2004), <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">Montenegro</a> (applied in 2008), <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Albania_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Albania to the European Union">Albania</a> (applied in 2009), and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">Serbia</a> (applied in 2009). All except Albania and Macedonia have started accession negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-albcand_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albcand-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macedonia_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macedonia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Kosovo_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Kosovo to the European Union">Kosovo</a>, whose independence is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">not recognised by five EU member states</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> are recognised as potential candidates for membership by the EU. <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> has formally submitted an application for membership, while Kosovo has a <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilisation and Association Agreement">Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> (SAA) with the EU, which generally precedes the lodging of membership application. In July 2014, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> announced that the EU has no plans to expand before 2019<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> while Serbia and Montenegro, the most advanced candidates, are expected to join before 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-before2025_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before2025-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> While the others are progressing, Turkish talks are at an effective standstill.<sup id="cite_ref-Hahn_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hahn-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The accession criteria are included in the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>, agreed in 1993, and the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Maastricht treaty">Treaty of Maastricht</a> (Article 49). Article 49 of the Maastricht Treaty (as amended) says that any "European state" that respects the "principles of liberty, democracy, respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms, and the rule of law", may apply to join the EU.  Whether a country is European or not is subject to <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria#Geographic_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">political assessment</a> by the EU institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-briefing23_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-briefing23-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">Past enlargement</a> has brought membership to twenty-eight members since the foundation of the European Union (EU) as the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> states in 1958.
</p><p>The three major <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">western European</a> countries that are not EU members, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Iceland_to_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of Iceland to the European Union">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Norway–European Union relations">Norway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Switzerland–European Union relations">Switzerland</a>, have all submitted membership applications in the past, but subsequently froze them. They do however, along with <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, participate in the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">EU Single Market</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, which makes them closely aligned with the EU. According to an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> strategy, the EU is unlikely to invite any more of its <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet</a> neighbours to join the bloc before 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-euobserver.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euobserver.com-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>  However, in 2014 the EU signed <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">Association Agreements</a> with <a href="/wiki/Georgia%E2%80%93European_Union_relations#Association_Agreement_(2013–2014)" title="Georgia–European Union relations">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Moldova–European Union Association Agreement">Moldova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Ukraine–European Union Association Agreement">Ukraine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_Sep_25,_2014_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_Sep_25,_2014-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> passed a resolution recognising the "European perspective" of all three countries.<sup id="cite_ref-EU_perspective_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_perspective-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div style="position:absolute; left:378px; top:252px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Iran–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>IRAN</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:366px; top:280px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Iraq%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Iraq–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>IRAQ</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:306px; top:300px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Israel–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>ISRAEL</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:338px; top:308px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Jordan%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Jordan–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>JORDAN</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:338px; top:172px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Kazakhstan–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>KAZAKHSTAN</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:334px; top:292px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Lebanon%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Lebanon–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>LEB.</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:246px; top:324px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Libya%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Libya–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>LIBYA</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:74px; top:308px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Morocco%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Morocco–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>MOROCCO</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:314px; top:312px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Palestine%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Palestine–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>PAL.</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:294px; top:152px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Russia–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>RUSSIA</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:334px; top:280px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Syria%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Syria–European Union relations"><span style="color:black"><b>SYRIA</b></span></a></span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:186px; top:308px"><span style="background:lightgrey"><a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union#Relations" title="Foreign relations of the European Union"><span style="color:black"><b>TUNISIA</b></span></a></span></div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;bottom:2px;right:2px;"><a href="/wiki/Template:EUNEARSTATES" title="Template:EUNEARSTATES"><img alt="Desc-i.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/10px-Desc-i.svg.png" width="10" height="10" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/15px-Desc-i.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/20px-Desc-i.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="648" /></a></div>
</div>
<p>The present enlargement agenda of the European Union regards <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkan" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Balkan">Western Balkan</a> states of <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. These states must negotiate the terms of their EU accession with the current member states, and align their domestic legislation with <a href="/wiki/EU_law" class="mw-redirect" title="EU law">EU law</a> before joining.
</p><p>Turkey has a long-standing application with the EU, but their negotiations are expected to take until at least 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This is due to the political issues surrounding the accession of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  As for the Western Balkan states, the EU had pledged to include them after their <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">civil wars</a>: in fact, two states have entered (<a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>), four are candidates and the others have pre-accession agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div style="position:absolute; left:306px; top:32px"><span style="color:white">ROMANIA</span></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:2px; top:316px">The European Union has made a commitment to accept the</div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:2px; top:332px">countries of the Western Balkans as full EU members</div>
</div>
<div style="position:absolute;bottom:2px;right:2px;"><a href="/wiki/Template:EUWESTBALKANS" title="Template:EUWESTBALKANS"><img alt="Desc-i.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/10px-Desc-i.svg.png" width="10" height="10" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/15px-Desc-i.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Desc-i.svg/20px-Desc-i.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="648" /></a></div>
</div>
<p>There are, however, other states in Europe which either seek membership or could potentially apply if their present foreign policy changes, or the EU gives a signal that they might now be included on the enlargement agenda. However, these are not formally part of the current agenda, which is already delayed due to bilateral disputes in the Balkans and difficulty in fully implementing the <i><a href="/wiki/Acquis_communautaire" title="Acquis communautaire">acquis communautaire</a></i> (the accepted body of EU law).
</p><p>In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> suggested in a strategy paper that the present enlargement agenda could potentially block the possibility of a future accession of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olli_Rehn" title="Olli Rehn">Olli Rehn</a> has said on occasion that the EU should "avoid overstretching our capacity, and instead consolidate our enlargement agenda," adding, "this is already a challenging agenda for our accession process."<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was previously the norm for enlargements to see multiple entrants join the Union at once. The only previous enlargements of a single state were the 1981 admission of Greece and the 2013 admission of Croatia.
</p><p>However, the EU members have warned that, following the significant impact of the fifth enlargement in 2004, a more individual approach will be adopted in the future, although the entry of pairs or small groups of countries will most probably coincide.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Balkans">Western Balkans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Western Balkans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2003 European Council summit in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> set integration of the Western <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> as a priority of EU expansion. This commitment was made in order to stabilise the region in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, a series of civil wars through the 1990s that led to the breakup of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, the first former Yugoslav country to obtain independence, <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">joined the EU in 2004</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> <a href="/wiki/2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2013 enlargement of the European Union">in 2013</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> are all candidate states, with Serbia and Montenegro in negotiations. <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> has applied to join but is not yet recognised as a candidate while <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, which declared independence in 2008, is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">not recognised by all EU states, or Serbia</a>. Serbia and Montenegro are expected to join before 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-before2025_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before2025-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Following the potential resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">Macedonia naming dispute</a>, Macedonia and Albania are expected to start talks by the end of 2019 and could also join by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Accession of Turkey to the European Union</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="European Union–Turkey relations">European Union–Turkey relations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg/220px-European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg.png" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg/330px-European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg/440px-European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Turkey_Locator.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Turkey shown in orange</div></div></div>
<p>Turkey's candidacy to join the EU has been a matter of major significance and considerable controversy since it was granted in 1999. Turkey has had historically close ties with the EU, having an <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Agreement" title="Ankara Agreement">association agreement since 1964</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> being in a <a href="/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93Turkey_Customs_Union" title="European Union–Turkey Customs Union">customs union with the EU</a> since 1995 and initially applying to join in 1987. Only after a summit in Brussels on 17 December 2004 (following the major <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">2004 enlargement</a>), the European Council announced that membership negotiations with Turkey were officially opened on 3 October 2005.
</p><p>Turkey is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">thirteenth largest economy in the world</a>, it has the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Armed_Forces" title="Turkish Armed Forces">second largest military force of NATO</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-economist2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and is a key <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Bildt" title="Carl Bildt">Carl Bildt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Foreign_Affairs_(Sweden)" title="Minister for Foreign Affairs (Sweden)">Swedish foreign minister</a>, stated that "[The accession of Turkey] would give the EU a decisive role for stability in the Eastern part of the Mediterranean and the Black Sea, which is clearly in the strategic interest of Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-ihtbildt_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ihtbildt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However others, such as former <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidents_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="List of presidents of France">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, maintain an opposition to Turkey's membership. Opponents argue that Turkey does not respect the key principles that are expected in a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracy</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of expression">freedom of expression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Turkey's large population would also alter the balance of power in the representative European institutions. Upon joining the EU, Turkey's 70&#160;million inhabitants would bestow it the second largest number of <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-economist2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Demographic projections indicate that Turkey would surpass Germany in the number of seats by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-economist2_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Turkey also does not recognise one EU state, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, over the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">Cyprus dispute</a> and the Cypriot government blocks some chapters of Turkey's talks in retaliation.
</p><p>Turkey's relations with the EU have seriously deteriorated in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2016 Turkish coup d&#39;état attempt">2016 Turkish coup d'état attempt</a> and subsequent <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Turkish_purges" class="mw-redirect" title="2016–17 Turkish purges">purges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 24 November 2016 the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> approved a non-binding resolution calling for the "temporary freeze of the ongoing accession negotiations with Turkey" over human rights and rule of law concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On 13 December, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> (comprising the heads of state or government of the member states) resolved that it would open no new areas in Turkey's membership talks in the "prevailing circumstances",<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> as Turkey’s path toward autocratic rule made progress on EU accession impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-Marc_Pierini_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marc_Pierini-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, and especially following Erdoğan's victory in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_constitutional_referendum,_2017" title="Turkish constitutional referendum, 2017">constitutional referendum</a>, Turkish accession talks are effectively at a standstill.<sup id="cite_ref-Hahn_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hahn-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-KOS-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-KOS_53-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008, but <a href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia&#39;s reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo has received formal recognition as an independent state from <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> out of 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>.  The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> remains divided on its policy towards Kosovo, with five <a href="/wiki/EU_member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="EU member states">EU member states</a> not recognizing its independence.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-AA-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AA_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">EU Association Agreement type: <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilisation and Association Agreement">Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> (SAA) for the Western <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> states participating in the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilisation and Association process">Stabilisation and Association process</a> of the EU (Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Macedonia, Montenegro, Serbia and Kosovo through the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_Tracking_Mechanism" title="Stabilisation Tracking Mechanism">STM</a>); <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">Association Agreement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Customs_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs Union">Customs Union</a> <a href="/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93Turkey_Customs_Union" title="European Union–Turkey Customs Union">for Turkey</a>; <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (EEA) for Iceland and Finland (reference state of the Fourth Enlargement); <a href="/wiki/Europe_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Europe Agreement">Europe Agreement</a> for the reference states of the Fifth Enlargement.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-MON-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MON_56-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> started negotiations in November 2005 while a part of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>.  Separate technical negotiations were conducted regarding issues of sub-state organizational competency.  A mandate for direct negotiations with Montenegro was established in July 2006.  Direct negotiations were initiated on 26 September 2006 and concluded on 1 December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-SER-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SER_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> started negotiations in November 2005 while part of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>, with a modified mandate from July 2006.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including anti-discrimination and equal opportunities for men and women.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="States_not_on_the_agenda">States not on the agenda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: States not on the agenda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">Foreign relations of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> (Article 49) states that any European country (as defined by a <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria#Geographic_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">European Council assessment</a>) that is committed to <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> may apply for membership in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Cfm_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cfm-78">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In addition to European states, other countries have also been speculated or proposed as future members of the EU.
</p><p>States in western Europe who have chosen, for various reasons, not to become full members of the EU have integrated with it to different extents according to their circumstances. Iceland, Norway and Liechtenstein participate directly in the single market via the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> does so via bilateral treaties and the other <a href="/wiki/European_microstates" title="European microstates">European microstates</a> have specific agreements with the EU and neighbouring countries, including their use of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as their currency. Most of these countries are also part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. While this integration is designed as a substitute for full membership, there are ongoing debates in a number of these countries as to whether they should join as full members. Three (Norway, Iceland and Switzerland) have all previously had live applications to join the EU which have been withdrawn or otherwise frozen. Such applications could be resubmitted in the event of a change in the political landscape.
</p><p>Georgia, Moldova and Ukraine ratified an Association Agreement with the EU and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> passed a resolution in 2014 stating that "in accordance with Article 49 of the Treaty on European Union, Georgia, Moldova and Ukraine, as well as any other European country, have a European perspective and can apply for EU membership in compliance with the principles of democracy, respect for fundamental freedoms and human rights, minority rights and ensuring the rule of rights."<sup id="cite_ref-en.trend.az_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.trend.az-79">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
<sup id="cite_ref-EU_perspective_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_perspective-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-en.trend.az_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.trend.az-79">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> They also entered the <a href="/wiki/Deep_and_Comprehensive_Free_Trade_Area" title="Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area">Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area</a> with the EU, that creates "framework for modernising [...] trade relations and for economic development by the opening of markets via the progressive removal of customs tariffs and quotas, and by an extensive harmonisation of laws, norms and regulations in various trade-related sectors, creating the conditions for aligning key sectors" of their economies with EU standards.<sup id="cite_ref-DCFTA_Ukr_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCFTA_Ukr-80">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_enlargement">Internal enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Internal enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">Withdrawal from the European Union</a></div>
<p>Internal enlargement is the process of new member states arising from the break-up of or secession from an existing member state.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> There have been and are a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_separatist_movements_in_Europe" title="List of active separatist movements in Europe">active separatist movements within member states</a> (for example in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independentism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan independentism">Catalonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Belgium" title="Partition of Belgium">Flanders</a>) but there are no clear agreements, treaties or precedents covering the scenario of an existing EU member state breaking into two or more states, both of which wish to remain EU member states. The question is whether one state is a successor and one a new applicant or, alternatively, both are new states which must be admitted to the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In some cases, a region desires to leave its state and the EU, namely those regions wishing to <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_Switzerland#Proposals_for_expansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlargement of Switzerland">join Switzerland</a>. But most, namely the two movements who have had referendums within the 2010s, Scotland and Catalonia, see their future as independent states within the EU. This results in great interest on whether, once independent, they would retain EU membership or conversely whether they would have to re-apply.  In the later case, since new members must be approved unanimously, any other state which has an interest in blocking their membership to deter similar independence movements could do so.<sup id="cite_ref-scot_apply_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scot_apply-123">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cat_pro_eu_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cat_pro_eu-124">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>  Additionally, it is unclear whether the successor state would retain any <a href="/wiki/Opt-outs_in_the_European_Union" title="Opt-outs in the European Union">opt-outs</a> that the parent state was entitled to.
</p>
<dl><dt>Opinions on membership</dt></dl>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union"><img alt="European Union" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a></span> <b>European Commission</b>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a>: “If there were to be a ‘yes’ vote in favour of Catalan independence, then we will respect that opinion. But Catalonia will not be able to be an EU member state on the day after such a vote.”<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> This was repeated in October in an official press release: <i>"We [...] reiterate the legal position held by this Commission as well as by its predecessors. If a referendum were to be organised in line with the Spanish Constitution it would mean that the territory leaving would find itself outside of the European Union."</i><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jose_Manuel_Barroso" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Manuel Barroso">Jose Manuel Barroso</a>, President of the European Commission (2004-2014), stated in 2012 in the context of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">2014 referendum for independence in Scotland</a>, that any new independent country would have to apply for membership and negotiate its terms, but that the <a href="/wiki/Rump_state" title="Rump state">rest of the original country</a> would not have to re-negotiate its position and would continue its membership.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-127">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>  In 2014 he said that it would have been 'very difficult' for an independent Scotland to join the EU, 'if not impossible', because of the difficulty of getting the approval of all member states, particularly Spain, which fears a possible secession of <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> and has blocked <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>'s accession to the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph16Feb2014a_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph16Feb2014a-129">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Almunia" class="mw-redirect" title="Joaquin Almunia">Joaquin Almunia</a> (former Spanish EU Commissioner) in 2013 claimed that Catalonia would have to apply for EU membership in the event of secession from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> <b>Government of Spain</b>
<ul><li>Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>, said in November 2013 that an independent Scotland's entry to the EU would require the consent of all existing members and that an independent Scotland or other regions gaining independence, taken as a reference to Catalonia, would end up outside of the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph-Rajoy_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-Rajoy-131">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scotsman03Feb2014a_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotsman03Feb2014a-132">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Spanish Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Garc%C3%ADa-Margallo_y_Marfil" class="mw-redirect" title="José García-Margallo y Marfil">José Garcia-Margallo</a>, having said in February 2012 that Spain would not veto Scottish accession to the EU, provided Scottish independence had UK agreement (thus making it different from Catalan independence),<sup id="cite_ref-Express26Feb2012a_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Express26Feb2012a-133">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <b>Government of the United Kingdom</b>
<ul><li>The UK Government's legal advice on the issue was that 'Since the [remainder of the UK] would be the same state as the UK, its EU membership would continue',<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> while speculating that 'On the face of it, Scotland would be required to accede to the EU as a new state, which would require negotiations on the terms of its membership ...', but that 'Scotland’s position within the EU is likely to be shaped more by any agreements between the parties than by pre-existing principles of EU law.'<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Without any formal process for handling the breakup of any member state, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> offered, if requested by a member state, to provide an official view on the EU's position on Scottish EU membership in the event of its independence from the UK. The Scottish Government requested that UK Prime Minister David Cameron place this request, but such a request was not made.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland"><img alt="Scotland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Flag_of_Scotland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Scotland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <b>Government of Scotland</b>
<ul><li>Deputy First Minister for Scotland, the SNP's <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Sturgeon" title="Nicola Sturgeon">Nicola Sturgeon</a>, said that the SNP Cabinet did not agree an independent Scotland would have to reapply for EU membership.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-127">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li><b>Referendum campaigns</b>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a>: The "Yes" campaign, led by <a href="/wiki/Blair_Jenkins" title="Blair Jenkins">Blair Jenkins</a>, argued that Scotland would continue as a member state following a Yes vote as Scotland would remain compliant with all EU Principles as outlined in <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Consolidated_version_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union/Title_I:_Common_Provisions" class="extiw" title="s:Consolidated version of the Treaty on European Union/Title I: Common Provisions">TEU Article 2</a> and there are no provisions to exclude a state in the existing EU agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> During the period between a Yes vote and formal independence, the Scottish Government could engage in negotiations, from within the EU, on the terms of their continuing membership in the EU. Several EU heads of state expressed their opinion that this position was reasonable, as did James Crawford, co-author of the UK government's legal advice on the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>  In an interview on BBC Radio, asked if the timescale of 18 months for EU and other treaty organisation was possible, Crawford replied that he felt the timescale was reasonable.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> However, there was no official comment on this view from the EU Commission. The Scottish <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a> Government and the Yes Campaign both declared that continuation of membership in the EU is their preference.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Better_Together_(campaign)" title="Better Together (campaign)">Better Together</a>: The "No" campaign, led by <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Darling" title="Alistair Darling">Alistair Darling</a>, argued that any vote for independence would have automatically placed Scotland out of the EU as a new state, and Scotland would have had to renegotiate entry.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scotland">Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">Scottish Independence Referendum of 2014</a> was the first occasion the EU was faced with the potential breakup of a member state, and one where the region declaring independence wished to retain its EU membership. While the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">UK's intentended withdrawal from the EU</a> would also take Scotland out of the EU, the debates in the referendum campaign may inform other future scenarios.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Catalonia">Catalonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Catalonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_movement" title="Catalan independence movement">Catalan independence movement</a></div>
<p>On 1 October 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan government">Catalan government</a> held a <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_referendum,_2017" title="Catalan independence referendum, 2017">referendum on independence</a>, which had been declared illegal by Spanish government, with potential polling stations being cordoned off by riot police. The subsequent events constituted a political crisis for Catalonia. The EU's position is to keep distance from the crisis while supporting Spain's territorial integrity and constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> While the debate around Scotland's referendum may inform the Catalan crisis, Catalonia is in a distinct situation from Scotland whereby the central government does not recognise the legitimacy of any independence declaration from Catalonia. If Spain does not recognise the independence of a Catalan state, both Catalonia cannot separately join the EU and it is still recognised as part of Spain's EU membership.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flanders">Flanders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flanders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Movement" title="Flemish Movement">Flemish Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Belgium" title="Partition of Belgium">Partition of Belgium</a></div>
<p>There is an active movement towards Flemish independence, or union with the Netherlands, with the future status of <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Wallonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_and_the_European_Union" title="Brussels and the European Union"><i>de facto</i> capital of the EU</a>)  unclear as viable political states, perhaps producing a unique situation from Scotland and Catalonia. There are various proposals for what should happen to the city, ranging from staying part of the Belgian rump state, to joining the hypothetical Flemish state, to becoming a separate political entity.<sup id="cite_ref-uclouvain_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uclouvain-143">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_state_expansion">Member state expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Member state expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Cyprus">Northern Cyprus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Northern Cyprus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus_and_the_European_Union" title="Northern Cyprus and the European Union">Northern Cyprus and the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_and_TRNC.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/EU_and_TRNC.png/250px-EU_and_TRNC.png" width="250" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/EU_and_TRNC.png/375px-EU_and_TRNC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/EU_and_TRNC.png/500px-EU_and_TRNC.png 2x" data-file-width="771" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_and_TRNC.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Area shown in orange under control of Northern Cyprus</div></div></div>
<p>Officially, the <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island nation</a> <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> is part of the European Union, under the <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> sovereignty of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Cyprus">Republic of Cyprus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots" title="Turkish Cypriots">Turkish Cypriots</a> are citizens of the Republic of Cyprus and thus of the European Union, and were entitled to vote in the 2004 <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2004" title="European Parliament election, 2004">European Parliament election</a> (though only a few hundred registered). The EU's <a href="/wiki/Acquis_communautaire" title="Acquis communautaire">acquis communautaire</a> is suspended indefinitely in the northern third of the island, which has remained outside the control of the Republic of Cyprus since the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkish invasion of 1974</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriot</a> community rejected the <a href="/wiki/Annan_Plan_for_Cyprus" title="Annan Plan for Cyprus">Annan Plan</a> for the settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">Cyprus dispute</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2004_Annan_Plan_Referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Annan Plan Referendum">referendum</a> on 24 April 2004. Had the referendum been in favour of the settlement proposal, the island (excluding the British <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign Base Areas">Sovereign Base Areas</a>) would have joined the European Union as the <i>United Cyprus Republic</i>. The European Union's relations with the <i>Turkish Cypriot Community</i> are handled by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s  <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Enlargement_(European_Commission)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Enlargement (European Commission)">Directorate-General for Enlargement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> has recognized that if the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">UK withdraws from the EU</a> as expected, then were <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> to be incorporated into <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> to form a <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">united Ireland</a> it would automatically rejoin the EU under Ireland's membership. This is consistent with the incorporation of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> as a single EU member state.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> A similar scenario has been envisioned with the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Romania_and_Moldova" title="Unification of Romania and Moldova">unification of Romania and Moldova</a>, which would incorporate the current territory of Moldova into Romania and thus into the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_territories_of_member_states">Special territories of member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Special territories of member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png/400px-European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png" width="400" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png/600px-European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png/800px-European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png 2x" data-file-width="2420" data-file-height="1292" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_OCTs_Locator.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3C62DD; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Member states of the European Union">Member states of the European Union</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #38DD6E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Current enlargement agenda</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #804000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">Special member state territories</a> outside the EU</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF8040; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic zone">EEZ</a> of <a href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">special member state territories</a> outside the EU</div></div></div></div>
<p>There are multiple <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_their_relations_with_the_EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Special member state territories and their relations with the EU">Special member state territories</a>, some of them are not fully covered by the EU treaties and apply EU law only partially, if at all. It is possible for a dependency to change its status regarding the EU or some particular treaty or law provision. The territory may change its status from participation to leaving or from being outside to joining.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_dependencies">British dependencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: British dependencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>British Overseas Territories</dt></dl>
<p>The only country with the status of <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">British Overseas Territory</a> that is part of the EU is <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, which joined the EEC together with the United Kingdom in 1973. The other overseas territories are defined as <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Countries_and_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Countries and Territories">Overseas Countries and Territories</a> of the EU. All of them are associated with the EU (meaning they apply some parts of EU law) and their nationals are in principle EU citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Crown Dependencies</dt></dl>
<p>Special terms were negotiated for the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> on the UK’s accession to the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>.  These are contained in Protocol 3 to the Treaty of Accession 1973.  The effect of the protocol is that the Channel Islands and the Isle of Man are within the Common Customs Area and the Common External Tariff (i.e. they enjoy access to European Union countries of physical exports without tariff barriers).  Other Community rules do not apply to the Islands.
</p>
<dl><dt>Sovereign Base Areas</dt></dl>
<p>The UK <a href="/wiki/UK_sovereign_base" class="mw-redirect" title="UK sovereign base">Sovereign Base Areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">Akrotiri and Dhekelia</a> on Cyprus did not join the European Union when the United Kingdom joined. <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2003" title="Treaty of Accession 2003">Cyprus' Accession Treaty</a> specifically stated that this would not change with the accession of Cyprus to the European Union. However, currently, some provisions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Law">EU Law</a> are applicable there—mainly <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a> management, <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">food safety</a> and free movement of people and goods.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish_self-governing_communities">Danish self-governing communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Danish self-governing communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>Faroe Islands</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_and_the_European_Union" title="Faroe Islands and the European Union">Faroe Islands and the European Union</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, a self-governing nation within the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>, are not part of the EU, as explicitly asserted by both Rome treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The relations with the EU are governed by a Fisheries Agreement (1977) and a <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Trade Agreement">Free Trade Agreement</a> (1991, revised 1998). The main reason for remaining outside the EU is disagreements about the <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">Common Fisheries Policy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> which disfavours countries with large fish resources. Also, every member has to pay for the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>, which favours countries having much agriculture which the Faroe Islands does not. When Iceland was in membership negotiations around 2010, there was a hope of better conditions for fish-rich countries, but this came to nothing. The Common Fisheries Policy was introduced in 1970 for the very reason of getting access for the first EC members into waters of candidate countries, UK, Ireland and Denmark with the Faroe Islands.
</p><p>Nevertheless, there are politicians, mainly in the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Union_Party_(Faroe_Islands)" title="Union Party (Faroe Islands)">Union Party</a> (<i>Sambandsflokkurin</i>), led by their chairman <a href="/wiki/Kaj_Leo_Johannesen" title="Kaj Leo Johannesen">Kaj Leo Johannesen</a>, who would like to see the Faroes as a member of the EU. However, the chairman of the left-wing <a href="/wiki/Republic_(Faroe_Islands)" title="Republic (Faroe Islands)">Republic</a> (<i>Tjóðveldi</i>), <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B8gni_Hoydal" title="Høgni Hoydal">Høgni Hoydal</a>, has expressed concerns that if the Faroes were to join the EU as is, they might vanish inside the EU, comparing this with the situation of the <a href="/wiki/Shetland_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetland Islands">Shetland Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land" class="mw-redirect" title="Åland">Åland</a> today, and wants the local government to solve the political situation between the Faroes and Denmark first.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Greenland</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenland_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenland and the European Union">Greenland and the European Union</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, a self-governing community that is part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>, entered the EC with Denmark in 1973, because it had no local independence at that time. After the establishment of Greenland's <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> in 1979 (effective from 1980), it held a second referendum on membership. The result was (mainly because of the Common Fisheries Policy) to leave, so on 1 February 1985, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> left the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a> and <a href="/wiki/EURATOM" class="mw-redirect" title="EURATOM">EURATOM</a>. Its status was changed to that of an Overseas Country.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Danish nationals residing in Greenland (i.e. all native population) are nonetheless fully European citizens; they are not, however, entitled to vote in European elections.
</p><p>There has been some speculation as to whether Greenland may consider rejoining the European Union. On 4 January 2007 the Danish daily <a href="/wiki/Jyllands-Posten" title="Jyllands-Posten">Jyllands-Posten</a> quoted the former Danish <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Greenland" title="Minister for Greenland">minister for Greenland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_H%C3%B8yem" title="Tom Høyem">Tom Høyem</a>, as saying "I would not be surprised if Greenland again becomes a member of the EU... The EU needs the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_window" class="mw-redirect" title="Arctic window">Arctic window</a> and Greenland cannot alone manage the gigantic Arctic possibilities".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Greenland has a lot of natural resources, and Greenland has, especially during the <a href="/wiki/2000s_commodities_boom" title="2000s commodities boom">2000s commodities boom</a>, contracted private companies to exploit some of them, but the cost is considered too high, as Greenland is remote and severely lacks infrastructure. After 2013 prices have declined so such efforts have stalled.
</p><p>The Brexit debate has reignited talk about the EU in Greenland, and there have been calls for the island to rejoin the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_constituent_countries_and_special_municipalities">Dutch constituent countries and special municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Dutch constituent countries and special municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The islands of <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> are constituent countries of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> are <a href="/wiki/BES_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="BES islands">special Dutch municipalities</a>. All are <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Countries_and_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Countries and Territories">Overseas Countries and Territories</a> (OCT) under Annex II of the EC treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> OCTs are considered to be "associated" with the EU and apply some portions of EU law. The islands are opting to become an <a href="/wiki/Outermost_regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Outermost regions">Outermost Region</a> (OMR) of the EU, the same status the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/French_overseas_departments" class="mw-redirect" title="French overseas departments">French overseas departments</a> have.
</p><p>When Bonaire, Sint Eustatius and Saba were established as Dutch public bodies after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles</a> (which was an OCT) in 2010, their status within the EU were raised. Rather than change their status from an OCT to an outermost region, as their change in status within the Netherlands would imply, it was decided that their status would remain the same for at least five years. After those five years, their status would be reviewed.
</p><p>If it was decided that one or all of the islands wish to integrate more with the EU then the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> provides for that following a unanimous decision from the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Enlargement" class="mw-redirect" title="European Commissioner for Enlargement">European Commissioner for Enlargement</a> <a href="/wiki/Danuta_H%C3%BCbner" title="Danuta Hübner">Danuta Hübner</a> has said before the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> that she does not expect many problems to occur with such a status change, as the population of the islands is only a few thousand people.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_overseas_departments_and_territories">French overseas departments and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: French overseas departments and territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The territories of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> are <i><a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department">overseas departments</a></i> of France and at the same time mono-departmental <i>overseas region</i>s. According to the EC treaty (article 299 2), all of these departments are <i><a href="/wiki/Outermost_regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Outermost regions">outermost regions</a></i> (OMR) of the EU—hence provisions of the EC treaty apply there while derogations are allowed. The status of the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_collectivity" title="Overseas collectivity">Overseas collectivity</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Martin" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Martin">Saint-Martin</a> is also defined as OMR by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>. New Caledonia and the overseas collectivities of French Polynesia, Saint-Barthelemy, Saint Pierre et Miquelon and Wallis and Futuna are <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Countries_and_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Countries and Territories">Overseas Countries and Territories</a> of the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>New Caledonia</dt></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_France" title="Overseas France">overseas territory</a> of France with its own unique status under the French Constitution, which is distinct from that of overseas departments and collectivities. It is defined as an "overseas country" under the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Noum%C3%A9a_Accord" title="Nouméa Accord">Nouméa Accord</a>, and enjoys a high degree of self-government.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Currently, in regard to the EU, it is one of the Overseas Countries and Territories (OCT).
</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Noum%C3%A9a_Accord" title="Nouméa Accord">Nouméa Accord</a>, New Caledonians will vote on an <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonian_independence_referendum,_2018" title="New Caledonian independence referendum, 2018">independence referendum</a> scheduled for November 2018. This referendum will determine whether the territory remains a part of the French Republic as a "sui generis collectivity", or whether it will become an independent state. The accords also specify a gradual devolution of powers to the local New Caledonian assembly.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008, but <a href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbia&#39;s reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo has received formal recognition as an independent state from <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> out of 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">member states</a>.</span>
</li>

Those <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaties of the EU">two Treaties</a> shall have the same legal value. The Union shall replace and succeed the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>".</span>
